        <p class="date">
         Fri Oct 12, 2007 at 07:54 PM PDT
        </p>
        <h2>
         <a href="/story/2007/10/13/397457/-Debbie-Schlussel-Decides-Who-The-True-Jews-Are" id="titleHref">
          Debbie Schlussel Decides Who The "True" Jews Are
         </a>
         <span style="white-space: nowrap">
         </span>
        </h2>
        <p class="author">
         <span>
          by
         </span>
         <a href="/user/Hunter">
          Hunter
         </a>
         <a alt="Follow this author" class="ajax type-user do-hotlist do-updateContent size-tiny off altTooltip" href="#?friend_id=1054&amp;is_stream=1">
          Follow
         </a>
         <span class="for">
          for
         </span>
         <a href="/blog/main">
          Daily Kos
         </a>
        </p>
        <ul class="front-page-share clearfix">
         <li style="margin-left: 0px">
          <div class="fb-share-button" data-href="http://www.dailykos.com/story/2007/10/13/397457/-Debbie-Schlussel-Decides-Who-The-True-Jews-Are" data-layout="button_count">
          </div>
         </li>
         <li>
          <a class="twitter-share-button" data-count="horizontal" data-related="markos" data-text='Debbie Schlussel Decides Who The "True" Jews Are' data-url="http://www.dailykos.com/story/2007/10/13/397457/-Debbie-Schlussel-Decides-Who-The-True-Jews-Are" data-via="dailykos" href="https://twitter.com/share">
           Tweet
          </a>
         </li>
         <li>
          <a class="comments comment_count_with_new" data-comment_count="207" data-story_id="397457" href="/story/2007/10/13/397457/-Debbie-Schlussel-Decides-Who-The-True-Jews-Are#comments">
           207 Comments
          </a>
         </li>
        </ul>
       </div>
       <div class="article-body">
        <div id="intro">
         <p>
          Still think there's not a conspiracy among conservatives to intentionally say the most stupid, offensive thing possible without getting Imus'ed?
         </p>
         <p>
          Well, "radio talk show host" Debbie Schlussel tops Coulter, and it's gotta be a secret contest, because there is no f--king way anyone is this damn stupid but still manages to chew their food. According to Schlussel,
          <a href="http://mediamatters.org/items/200710130001">
           if you're Jewish and offended by Ann Coulter's statements, you're a phony Jew
          </a>
          :
         </p>
         <blockquote>
          <p>
           True religious Jews are not offended by Ann [Coulter]'s comments, though they really appreciate her alliance with our causes. It's only the Jewish libs, like Deutch [sic], who are feigning this shock and outrage. That's because she's a threat to their real religion: liberalism.
          </p>
         </blockquote>
         <p>
          Of course, Schlussel makes a big point of saying that
          <em>
           she
          </em>
          is a true "religious Jew", and
          <em>
           other
          </em>
          Jews are the phony ones, so it's not a bigoted statement -- of course not.
         </p>
         <p>
          The reason I keep bringing these things up, this week, is to show this as standard operating procedure
          <em>
           throughout
          </em>
          the right. It shouldn't be ignored, it should be highlighted. This is the entire nut of their movement: deciding which soldiers are
          <em>
           patriotic
          </em>
          , and which ones are
          <em>
           phony
          </em>
          . Deciding which families living in the aftereffects of tragedy are
          <em>
           needy
          </em>
          , and which are
          <em>
           phony
          </em>
          . Deciding which Jews are
          <em>
           true
          </em>
          , and which are
          <em>
           phony
          </em>
          . "Phony" is the mantra: anyone who disagrees with them is either (1) mentally ill, (2) under the spell of evil liberals, or (3) frauds. They seem to revel in thier own incapacity to comprehend dissent.
         </p>
         <p>
          But I have no explanation for this current round of unusually spectacular conservative crap, other than perhaps the melting icecaps have released all the excess Stupid that was trapped in ancient ice as the dinosaurs died off.
         </p>
        </div>
        <div class="article-body" id="body">
        </div>
       </div>

          <p>
           <b>
            More Tagging tips:
           </b>
          </p>
          <p>
           A tag is a way to search for this diary. If someone is searching for "Barack Obama," is this a diary they'd be trying to find?
          </p>
          <p>
           Use a person's full name, without any title. Senator Obama may become President Obama, and Michelle Obama might run for office.
          </p>
          <p>
           If your diary covers an election or elected official, use election tags, which are generally the state abbreviation followed by the office. 
		CA-01 is the first district House seat. CA-Sen covers both senate races. NY-GOV covers the New York governor's race.
          </p>
          <p>
           Tags do not compound: that is, "education reform" is a completely different tag from "education". A tag like "reform" alone is probably not meaningful.
          </p>

           <li id="c174">
            <div class="cx" id="cx14054323">
             <h5>
              <a class="de">
              </a>
              <span class="cu">
               I can't agree with the way that Debbie puts it
              </span>
              <span class="crd ntb">
               (
               <a href="/comments/397457/14054323#c174?mode=alone;showrate=1#c174">
                1+ / 0-
               </a>
               )
              </span>
             </h5>
             <div class="crs">
              <dl>
               <dt>
                Recommended by:
               </dt>
               <dd>
                <a href="/user/uid:92910">
                 vets74
                </a>
               </dd>
              </dl>
             </div>
             <div class="ct">
              <p>
               In part, because she truly is a crazy Ann Coulter wannabe but is too stupid and unappealing to pull off the act.
              </p>
              <p>
               But it struck me that I have heard similar musings to Coulters in the distant past, from Alan Berg, the Denver talk radio show host who was gunned down in the early 1980's. Berg, who was Jewish, used to have a segment on his show entitled "Talk to a Jew" - - clearly parody, and very funny, but also serious and disturbing. And his show contained a lot of irreverence towards Jews, and comparisons between Christians and Jews and so on.
              </p>
              <p>
               In this case, I don't really think Coulter was all that out of line. She was trying to be funny. Her credentials are such that nothing that she can say will be amusing to me. But her references to camel jockeys and exterminating Muslims (sentiments that Ms. Schlussel shares, by the way), strike me as far more offensive.
              </p>
              <p>
               Ultimately, it would be nice if we could just stop thinking about people like Ann Coulter - - or perhaps consign them to having the relevance of the senile rantings of prominent conservatives like Art Linkletter.
              </p>
             </div>
             <div class="cf">
              <p class="sig">
              </p>

            <span class="crd ntb">
             (
             <a href="/comments/397457/14051829#c34?mode=alone;showrate=1#c34">
              5+ / 0-
             </a>

           <div class="ct">
            <p>
             ...than debates over who the "true" christians or who the "true" progressives are.
            </p>
            <p>
             While far more popular a tactic on the right, this tactic is not seen exclusively on the right.
            </p>
           </div>
           <div class="cf">
            <p class="sig">
            </p>
            <p class="cb">

             <a href="/user/uid:4633">

         <li id="c126">
          <div class="cx" id="cx14052879">
           <h5>
            <a class="de">
            </a>
            <span class="cu">
             There's been a quiet disagreement over
            </span>
            <span class="crd ntb">
             (
             <a href="/comments/397457/14052879#c126?mode=alone;showrate=1#c126">
              5+ / 0-
             </a>
             )
            </span>
           </h5>
           <div class="crs">
            <dl>
             <dt>
              Recommended by:
             </dt>
             <dd>
              <a href="/user/uid:23276">
               Bensdad
              </a>
              ,
              <a href="/user/uid:44504">
               madaprn
              </a>
              ,
              <a href="/user/uid:54668">
               jfadden
              </a>
              ,
              <a href="/user/uid:71897">
               isis2
              </a>
              ,
              <a href="/user/uid:76355">
               ER Doc
              </a>
             </dd>
            </dl>
           </div>
           <div class="ct">
            <p>
             who's really a Jew for quite a while. Unlike this Debbie nut (I'm not going to bother to spell her last name) most Jews on both/all sides of the debate have tried to keep the disagreements at the level of a quiet truce. Orthodox Jews, a minority of Jews in the USA, have almost complete control of deciding who is a Jew in most countries that have established religions. Generally, if your mother's mother's ... mother's mother was ethnically Jewish, you qualify as Jewish even if you're first assistant to Osama bin Laden, never knew you could be considered Jewish, and don't want to be Jewish.
             <br/>
             Orthodox Rabbis and authorities don't generally recognize conversions by Reform or Conservative Rabbis,
             <em>
              except Israel recognizes those conversions if they were done
              <strong>
               outside
              </strong>
              Israel -- but not if they were done
              <strong>
               inside
              </strong>
              Israel
             </em>
             . In fact, Moslems such as Arabs living in Israel have more religious rights than Reform and Conservative Jews living there who want to practice Reform or Conservative Judaism. For example, a Moslem marriage has legal standing in Israel, but the last I heard, a marriage by a Reform or Conservative Rabbi done in Israel has no legal standing there.
            </p>
            <p>
             I think most if not all religious traditions have some fundamentalist branches. Lately the fundamentalist Christians and Jews have been banding together, and they have a sort of symbiotic, mutual hate relationship with fundamentalist Moslems -- they hate each other, but they need each other because hate is an important motivating force on both/all sides.
            </p>
            <p>
             I've come to think that fundamentalism or openness is the most important aspect of a particular branch of a religion, and the theological roots that branch may claim are irrelevant. I'd rather associate with a tolerant worshipper of the Flying Spaghetti Monster than a fundamentalist member of my "own" religion -- like crazy Debbie.
            </p>
           </div>
           <div class="cf">
            <p class="sig">

             </span>

             <p>

             <p>
              Religious fundamentalism is kind of like fire. It can get out of control, but burning houses are not inherent in its nature. Religious fundamentalists may offend our sensibilities, but they're not a problem, provided they aren't proselytic (and Jewish fundamentalists do not proselytize).
             </p>
             <p>
              Wingnut religious fundamentalism, though, is
              <em>
               extremely
              </em>
              dangerous. It's fire inching its way toward a nearly empty gas can. (And if you have ever played with fire, you know that this is more dangerous than a full one.)
             </p>

            <blockquote>
             <p>
              3 you shall have no other gods before me.
             </p>
             <p>
              4 You shall not make for yourself an idol, whether in the form of anything that is in heaven above, or that is on the earth beneath, or that is in the water under the earth.
             </p>
             <p>
              5 You shall not bow down to them or worship them; for I the Lord your God am a jealous God, punishing children for the iniquity of parents, to the third and the fourth generation of those who reject me,
             </p>
             <p>
              6 but showing steadfast love to the thousandth generation of those who love me and keep my commandments.
             </p>
            </blockquote>
            <p>
             She worships at a Republican altar, and it leads her into error.

           <p>
            Christian relations with Israel, however, are paramount because of millenarian eschatology, and, by extension, a patronizingly paternal and self-serving view of Jews as the covenant people. When Schlussel talks about "true" religious Jews, that's fundie code for those 100% dedicated to the uncritical acceptance of Israel and its formation as a nation-state to fulfill God's plan for the end of the world; subsequently the code further endorses "true Christians" as those who support Israel uncritically along with America as its divinely anointed protector. For in the End, "true Christians" will become the "true Jews" as heirs of the realized covenant of Christ.
           </p>
           <p>

           </p>
           <p>
            Kossacks who find her exceptional in her offense woefully underestimate the staggering scale of ideologically inspired ignorance that stands between us and the realization of progressive goals for American society as a whole.

           <span class="crd ntb">
            (
            <a href="/comments/397457/14054674#c179?mode=alone;showrate=1#c179">
             0+ / 0-
            </a>

           </span>
          </h5>
          <div class="ct">
           <p>
            to prove
            <em>
             any
            </em>
            religious theory. Don't these people realize that we all have access to the same source material and they look mighty foolish trying to define something they know so little about? I wonder if any of these religious bigots have even read the Bible they pretend to quote.
           </p>
           <p>
            It isn't even a new trick; Germany was dividing the Jews into "good" Jews and "bad" Jews before Kristallnacht ever took place. So it isn't much of a stretch for "good Jew" Schlussel to accept Colter's ideology of a "bad Jew".
           </p>
           <p>
            It's beginning to remind one of the ol' South under the white sheets, isn't it? You'd think they would be clever enough to realize that connecting religious and racial intolerance would invoke the ghosts of history past.
           </p>

  <script type="text/javascript">
   if($.cookie('meter_user') !== 'false') {
		if ($('#ePostButton').length &gt; 0) {
		  $('#ePostButton').click(function() { 
		    DailyKos.Metrics.track('Posted Comment', { 
		      repliedTo: $(this).parents('#eP').prevAll('.cb').children('a').first().html() 
		    });
		  });
		}
		
		if (!!document.location.pathname.match('activate') &amp;&amp; $('h1:contains("Welcome to Daily Kos!")').length &gt; 0) {
		  DailyKos.Metrics.track('Signed Up');
		}
		
		if (document.location.pathname === '/') {
		  if (document.location.hostname.match(/^www|^dailykos/)) {
		    DailyKos.Metrics.track('Viewed Front Page');
		  } else {
		    var subdomain = document.location.hostname.split('.')[0];
		    DailyKos.Metrics.track('Viewed Vertical', { name: subdomain });
		  }
		}
		
		if ($('.ratinate').length &gt; 0) {
		  $('.ratinate').click(function() { DailyKos.Metrics.track('Recommended Comment') });
		}
		
		if ($('.do-addRating.type-story').length &gt; 0) {
		  $('.do-addRating.type-story').click(function() { DailyKos.Metrics.track('Recommended Story') });
		}
		
		if ($("form[action$='publishHow']").length &gt; 0) {
		  $(document).ready(function() {
			  $('.type-story.do-publishHow').click(function() { DailyKos.Metrics.track('Published Story') });
			 });
		}
		
		if (document.location.pathname.match(/^\/user/) &amp;&amp; $('li.here').length &gt; 0) {
		  if ($('.pageMenu:first li.here').children('a').html().match(/Stream/)) {
		    DailyKos.Metrics.track('Viewed Stream', { name: $('.name').children('a').html() });
		  } else if ($('.pageMenu:first li.here').children('a').html().match(/Profile/)) {
		    DailyKos.Metrics.track('Viewed Profile', { name: $('.name').children('a').html() });
		  } else if ($('.pageMenu:last li.here').children('a').html().match(/My Recent Replies/)) {
		    DailyKos.Metrics.track('Viewed Replies');
		  }
		} 
		
		if ($('#search-tabbed').length &gt; 0) {
		  DailyKos.Metrics.track('Searched');
		}
		
		if ($('#group-tables').length &gt; 0) {
			DailyKos.Metrics.track('Viewed Groups List');
		}
		
		if (document.location.pathname.match(/^\/groups/) &amp;&amp; $("#group_info").length &gt; 0) {
		  DailyKos.Metrics.track('Viewed Group', { name: $('.name').children('a').text() });
		}
		
		if ($('.do-hotlist.type-user, .do-unHotlist.type-user').length &gt; 0) {
		  $('.do-hotlist.type-user, .do-unHotlist.type-user').click(function() {
		    var nickName;
		    nickName = ($(this).prev('a').html() || $('.name a').html())
		    if ($(this).hasClass('do-hotlist')) {
		      DailyKos.Metrics.track('Followed User', { nickname: nickName }) 
		    } else if ($(this).hasClass('do-unHotlist')) {
		      DailyKos.Metrics.track('Unfollowed User', { nickname: nickName }) 
		    }    
		  });
		}
	}
  </script>
